Argument from Opposing Natures
Maturidi uses the coexistence of fire/heat and cold to prove a wise manager.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the coexistence of opposing natural properties like heat and cold in one body points to a wise and powerful manager.

Core Idea
Opposing natures cannot unite without an external wise controller.

Maturidi begins with a simple observation: heat rises, cold descends, yet they combine in a single living body. This cannot happen by nature alone; it demands a manager who overrules these tendencies. In this lesson, you will see how this everyday fact leads to the affirmation of a powerful, knowing Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Note the contrast between the natural tendencies and their unity.
2
Identify the two opposing natures
The passage mentions heat (rising) and cold (descending). Observe how Maturidi uses their natural opposition to set up the argument.
3
Reflect on the logical inference
The conclusion 'that this is because of a manager, subjugator, knowing' is not stated as a proof but as an immediate inference. Ask yourself: why can't nature itself cause this unity?
The key is that opposite natures would repel each other, so something external must force them together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد نجا الحرارة ترتفع بطبعها والبرودة تنحدر وقد يجتمعان في جسم، فثبت أن ذلك لمدير قاهر عليم. ومن يقول بقدم الأعيان فوجدناها غير خالية عن الحوادث لمنع القبول بذلك لوجوه: أحدها في القدم خلاء، وفى ذلك تكذيب شهادة العيان، والثانى وجود كثير من الأعيان وابتداؤها لمدد تعد، وهى من آخر الجملة تحتمل ما يحتمل الكل لذلك لزم القول، ولم يجز أن يقال: كان كامنا فظهر أو متفرقا فاجتمع لما فيه اثبات غير حكم العيان، وإذا احتمل ذلك، و إن ارتفع عن الإحاملة به، احتمل كون العالم من لا شيء، وإن ارتفع وجوده عن توهم البشر بدليل، والكمون لا يحتمل لإحالة كون شيء واحد مكانا لعشرة مثله، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ولما لا يخلو العيان وصفته من صور، ثم لا يخلو من مصور، كسائر ما يضيفها الناسخ على هامش النص وبها تستقيم العبارة.
And indeed heat rises by its nature and cold descends, yet they may combine in one body. So it is established that this is because of a manager, subjugator, knowing. And whoever says that substances (a'yan) are eternal, we find them not free from originated accidents, which prevents acceptance, for several reasons: one, there is emptiness in eternity, and that is a denial of the testimony of observation; second, the existence of many substances and their beginning for counted durations, and they are from the end of the sum that what the whole can bear, therefore the statement is necessary. And it is not permissible to say: 'It was hidden and then appeared' or 'dispersed and then gathered' because that implies affirming other than the judgment of observation. And if that can be assumed, even if its assumption is far-fetched, then it can be assumed that the world came from nothing, even if its existence is beyond human imagination by proof. And hiddenness (kumun) is not admissible because it is impossible that one thing becomes a place for ten like it. There is no power except with God. And since observation and its description are not devoid of forms, then it is not devoid of a form-giver, like the rest of what the copyist adds on the margin of the text and by which the expression is correct.
Source pages p. 716

Commentary
This passage contains two arguments. First, Maturidi points to the observable fact that heat rises and cold sinks by their natural tendencies, yet they coexist in a single body (e.g., a living organism). This harmony cannot be explained by nature alone; it requires a wise manager (mudabbir qahir 'alim) who overrides natural tendencies. Second, he refutes the eternity of substances (a'yan). He argues that substances are never free from originated accidents (hawadith), so they must themselves be originated. He rejects the theory of 'kumun' (hiddenness) which claims that substances pre-exist in a hidden state and then appear, because that would imply contradiction—e.g., one thing becoming a place for ten. The argument concludes that if substances are originated, then the world's existence from nothing is plausible. Finally, he notes that forms (suwar) require a form-giver (musawwir).

Key Terms
حرارة (heat)
برودة (cold)
مدير (manager)
قاهر (subjugator)
عليم (knowing)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument from opposites is purely physical and can be explained by natural processes.
Correction: Maturidi's argument is metaphysical: it relies on the impossibility of contradictory natures forcing unity without an external agent. Natural processes themselves have opposite tendencies, so their coordination points to a wise director.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the coexistence of rising heat and descending cold in one body prove?
A) That nature is stronger than we think
B) That there is a wise manager who controls natures
C) That heat and cold are not real
D) That substances are eternal

Key Takeaway
The observable unity of opposites in nature points to a wise manager who overrides natural tendencies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You witness heat and cold coexisting in your own body. But what about the contradictions in your soul—the pull towards sin and the pull towards righteousness? Do you actively entrust their management to the All-Knowing Manager, or do you try to manage them yourself and fail? Will you surrender that struggle to Him today?
?
The Subjugator (Qahir) overpowers natural tendencies. Is there an area of your life where your natural inclinations have overcome your faith—like laziness, anger, or desire? Have you sincerely asked the Subjugator to overpower them in you? What specific step will you take to invite His subjugation?
?
The Manager knows (Alim) how to combine opposites. You know your own weaknesses and strengths. Do you trust that Allah's knowledge of how to manage your life is greater than your own planning? What worry or plan will you release to His management right now?

Refuting the Eternity of Substances
Maturidi gives two reasons against eternal substances and refutes the hiddenness theory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi argument against the eternity of substances by showing they are never free from originated accidents, and the refutation of the hiddenness (kumun) theory.

Core Idea
Nothing that always has changes can be eternal.

Maturidi now takes on a key rival view: that substances (a'yan) are eternal. He points out that substances are never found without originated accidents, which means they cannot be eternal. He also refutes the theory of hiddenness (kumun) as an alternative explanation. This lesson unpacks these crucial arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two distinct objections listed with 'one' and 'second'.
The passage is denser; take your time.
2
Identify the two reasons against eternity
First reason: eternal substances would be empty of accidents in pre-eternity, contradicting observation. Second: many substances have a clear beginning in time, so they are not eternal.
3
Understand the rejection of kumun
The theory of hiddenness says substances pre-exist and then appear. Maturidi rejects it because it would imply that one thing can become the place for many, which is impossible. Also, he shows that if kumun were possible, then creation from nothing would also be possible, undermining the opponent's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Misconception: The argument against eternal substances relies only on the occurrence of accidents.

?

?

Argument from Forms for a Form-Giver
Maturidi argues that forms require a form-giver.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all observed forms require a form-giver, leading to the affirmation of Allah as Musawwir (the Form-Giver).

Core Idea
Every form points to a form-giver.

In the final part of this passage, Maturidi uses a simple but powerful observation: every observed form must have a form-giver. Just as we see patterns in nature that indicate a maker, the existence of forms (suwar) in the world necessitates a Designer. This lesson highlights the argument from design at a fundamental level.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. This is a short but complete argument.
The last part about the copyist may be a scribal addition; focus on the core reasoning.
2
Identify the key premise
Maturidi states that observation and its description are never devoid of forms. This means every observed thing has a form.
3
Draw the inference to a form-giver
If forms exist, they must come from a source that gives forms. Just as any designed object implies a designer, forms imply a form-giver (musawwir).
This is a straightforward a posteriori argument for God as the origin of all forms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

This harmony cannot be explained by nature alone; it requires a wise manager (mudabbir qahir 'alim) who overrides natural tendencies. Second, he refutes the eternity of substances (a'yan). He argues that substances are never free from originated accidents (hawadith), so they must themselves be originated. He rejects the theory of 'kumun' (hiddenness) which claims that substances pre-exist in a hidden state and then appear, because that would imply contradiction—e.g., one thing becoming a place for ten. The argument concludes that if substances are originated, then the world's existence from nothing is plausible. Finally, he notes that forms (suwar) require a form-giver (musawwir).

Key Terms
صور (forms)
مصور (form-giver)
عيان (observation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Forms can exist without a form-giver, like random patterns in nature.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the very existence of forms (which are meaningful and structured) necessitates a source that imparts form, just as a written text requires a writer.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is never devoid of forms?
A) The intellect
B) Observation and its description
C) The form-giver
D) The hiddenness

Key Takeaway
The existence of forms in the world necessitates a form-giver, establishing Allah as Musawwir.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the forms around you—your own body, the trees, the stars—do you truly see them as signs of a Creator, or have you become numb to their testimony? If you were to take Maturidi's argument seriously today, what would you change about how you observe the world?
?
If every form requires a form-giver, then your own existence as a formed being demands that you acknowledge Allah as Musawwir. Are you living in a way that reflects that recognition? What is one tangible action you will take this week to remind yourself that you are a created, formed being?
?
The analogy of the scribe reminds us that every text has an author. Your life is a text—what does it say about the Author? Does the form of your daily actions correspond to the form of belief in the Form-Giver? Ask yourself sincerely: have you treated your own existence as an accidental form without meaning, or as a purposeful creation?

The Principle of Natures and Their Need for an Origin
Maturidi establishes that natures need an origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi proves the existence of an origin (منشئ) for natural substances based on the principle that natures only act on prepared recipients.

Core Idea
Natures do not cause themselves; their need for a recipient proves an origin.

Maturidi begins his argument by examining how natural substances operate. He observes that any nature only affects something that is suitably prepared to receive its influence. This principle, he argues, shows that natures themselves are not self-sufficient but require an external origin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on 'كل ذي طبع'
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the examples of pain, pleasure, and dyes.
These examples illustrate how a nature only acts on something that can accept its effect.
2
Identify the key principle
Maturidi states that it is not the work of nature to make something accept its nature. This implies that natures are not self-originating.
3
Understand the conclusion
The passage concludes that the existence of natures points to an origin (منشئ) beyond them.
This is the first step in the larger argument for a director.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم كل ذي طبع لا يعمل في شيء بطبعه إلا أن يكون الآخر مجعولا بحيث يقبل ذلك، نحو الشيء الذي يتأذى لا يؤذيه الفعل الذي في غيره مؤذ، وكذلك المؤلم والملذ، وكذلك الأصباغ. وليس عمل الطبع أن يجعل شيئا يقبل طبعه ويتأثر به، فثبت به كون غير الطبائع. مع ما لو خلى بين ذي الطبع وعمله لكان لا يؤلف ولا يصور، فدل وجودها على غير ذلك: أن لها منشئا. وبعد، فإنه لو خلى بين الأصباغ وانصباغ الأشياء بها ليخرج فاسدا مسمما وإنما يصلح ذلك الحكيم العليم يضع كل شيء موضعه، فمثله أمر الطبائع وهو في شأن الطبائع أحق؛ إذ هي تتنافر وفيها التباعد، أو يقدح في الأشياء بلا حد، وفيه الفساد، فدل الاتساق وقيام الأعيان بها على عليم قاهر جمع بينها ما كان لكل مجتمع الطبائع حامل يحملها ليس هو لهن، فثبت بالضرورة وجودهن. وقد نجا الحرارة ترتفع بطبعها والبرودة تنحدر وقد يجتمعان في جسم، فثبت أن ذلك لمدير قاهر عليم.
Then every possessor of a nature does not act in anything by its nature unless the other is made such that it accepts that, like a thing that is hurt does not hurt it by an action that is hurtful in another, and likewise the painful and the pleasurable, and likewise dyes. And it is not the work of nature to make something accept its nature and be affected by it, so the existence of non-natures is established. With that, if one left between the possessor of a nature and its work, it would not compose nor form, so their existence indicates something else: that they have an origin. And furthermore, if one left between dyes and the dyeing of things with them, it would come out corrupt and poisonous, but only the wise All-Knowing sets everything in its place, and likewise the matter of natures, and He is more entitled in the affair of natures, since they repel each other and have distance, or it would strike at things without limit, and in that is corruption. So the harmony and the subsistence of entities by them indicate a knowing Compeller who brought them together, that every aggregate of natures has a carrier that carries them not being one of them, so their existence is necessarily established. And indeed heat rises by its nature and cold descends, yet they meet in a body, so it is established that that is due to a powerful knowing Director.
Source pages p. 716

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the existence of a wise, powerful director based on the behavior of natural substances. Maturidi begins by observing that anything with a nature only acts upon something that is prepared to receive its effect. For example, a painful thing only hurts something that can feel pain. This shows that natures themselves do not originate action arbitrarily; they require suitable recipients. He then argues that if left to themselves, natures would not produce orderly forms or compositions—they would cause disorder. For instance, if dyes were left without a wise dyer, they would produce poisonous results. Similarly, the various conflicting natures, which repel each other, could not harmoniously coexist without a wise Compeller who brings them together and sustains them in a single body. As a specific example, heat naturally rises and cold naturally descends, yet they coexist in a single body. This impossible without a director who is both powerful and knowing. Thus, the argument concludes that there must be a directing agent beyond the natures themselves.

Key Terms
طبع (nature)
منشئ (origin)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the principle that a nature only acts on a prepared recipient prove?
A) That natures are self-sufficient
B) That natures have an origin beyond themselves
C) That pain and pleasure are the same
D) That dyes can mix without a dyer

Key Takeaway
Natures depend on prepared recipients, proving they are not ultimate and require an origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever rely on your own nature—your intelligence, strength, or habits—as if they are self-sufficient, forgetting that they cannot even act without Allah preparing the circumstances? What would it take for you to genuinely feel your absolute dependence on Him every moment?
?
When you achieve something, do you attribute it solely to your own effort and nature, or do you recognize that your nature only works because Allah prepared the recipient and the conditions? Will you start your next task with a conscious acknowledgment that 'if left alone, my nature would not compose or form'?
?
The passage says natures do not create their recipients. Think of a talent or ability you have: did you create the capacity to receive and use it? How does this truth change the way you view your own gifts and the Giver?

Proof from Dyes and the Coexistence of Heat and Cold
Maturidi proves a wise director through dyes and the coexistence of heat and cold.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how Maturidi uses the examples of dyes and the coexistence of heat and cold to demonstrate the need for a wise, knowing director.

Core Idea
Opposites like heat and cold cannot combine without a powerful director.

After establishing that natures need an origin, Maturidi presents two striking examples. First, dyes left to themselves would produce poisonous results, requiring a wise arranger. Second, heat and cold naturally separate but coexist in bodies, pointing to a director who overrides nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the dye analogy
Read the passage about dyes and the translation. Notice that without a wise dyer, dyes would produce corruption.
The dye analogy shows that a wise agent is needed to bring harmony.
2
Understand the harmony proof
Maturidi extends the dye analogy to all natures: they repel each other, yet entities subsist harmoniously, indicating a Compeller who brought them together.
3
Examine the heat and cold example
Heat rises and cold descends by nature, yet they meet in a single body. This impossible without a powerful knowing director.
This is the climax of the argument.

Misconception: The coexistence of opposites in nature proves that natures can combine by themselves.

?

?

The Two Arguments Against the Eternity of Bodies
Maturidi enumerates two arguments against the eternity of bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's two main arguments against the eternity of bodies based on observation and the beginnings of individual entities.

Core Idea
Observation shows bodies change; eternity can't contain change.

Maturidi begins his refutation by directly addressing the claim that entities (bodies) are eternal. He provides two clear reasons: first, that eternity would be empty of the changes we observe, and second, that many entities have definite beginnings, implying the whole does too. This lesson focuses on these foundational arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting Maturidi's concise style.
Pay attention to the two reasons introduced by 'أحدها' and 'الثاني'.
2
Identify the first reason
The first reason is that eternity is empty of accidents, but we observe bodies are never free from accidents. This contradicts the testimony of observation.
Think about what 'testimony of observation' means here.
3
Identify the second reason
The second reason is that we see many entities beginning to exist at specific times. These later entities share the same nature as the whole, so the whole must also have a beginning.
The phrase 'من آخر الجملة' refers to these later entities as part of the aggregate.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that the statement (that bodies are not eternal) is necessary. Consider why these two reasons are sufficient to reject the claim of eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن يقول بقدم الأعيان فوجدناها غير خالية عن الحوادث لمنع القبول بذلك لوجوه: أحدها في القدم خلاء، وفي ذلك تكذيب شهادة العيان، والثاني وجود كثير من الأعيان وابتداؤها لمدد تعد، وهي من آخر الجملة تحتمل ما يحتمل الكل لذلك لزم القول، ولم يجز أن يقال: كان كامنا فظهر أو متفرقا فاجتمع لما فيه إثبات غير حكم العيان، وإذا احتمل ذلك، وإن ارتفع عن الإحاملة به، احتمل كون العالم من لا شيء، وإن ارتفع وجوده عن توهم البشر بدليل، والكمون لا يحتمل لإحالة كون شيء واحد مكانا لعشرة مثله، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ولما لا يخلو العيان وصفته من صور، ثم لا يخلو من مصور.
And whoever says that entities are eternal, we find them not free from accidents, which prevents acceptance of that, for several reasons: one is that in eternity there is emptiness, and in that is a denial of the testimony of observation; the second is the existence of many entities and their beginning at countable periods, and they are from the end of the aggregate and are subject to what the whole is subject to, therefore the statement is necessary. And it is not permissible to say: they were latent and appeared, or scattered and gathered, because that involves affirming something other than the judgment of observation. And if that is possible, even if it is raised above being burdened by it, the possibility of the world coming from nothing arises, even if its existence is raised above human imagination by evidence. And latency is not possible because it is inconceivable that one thing becomes a place for ten things like it. And there is no power except with God. And since observation and its description are never free from forms, then they are never free from a form-giver.
Source pages p. 716

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that bodies (entities) are eternal (qadim). Maturidi argues that we observe bodies are never free from accidents (hawadith), which are temporal. Therefore, they cannot be eternal. He gives two reasons: (1) Eternity is empty of temporal events, but we see bodies changing, so observation contradicts eternity. (2) Many entities have definite beginnings in time, and the later ones share the same properties as the whole, so the whole must also have a beginning. He then refutes the alternative explanations that bodies might have been latent and then appeared, or were scattered and then gathered, because these explanations contradict direct observation. Moreover, if latency were posited, that would open the possibility that the world could come from nothing, which is absurd, because latency would require one thing to be the place for many, which is impossible. Finally, he adds that since every observed thing has a form, it must have a form-giver, implying a creator.

Key Terms
قدم (eternity)
أعيان (entities)
حوادث (accidents/events)
شهادة العيان (testimony of observation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because bodies always exist, they must be eternal, ignoring that they are always accompanied by changing accidents.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the presence of accidents itself disproves eternity, as eternity cannot contain change.

Checkpoint
According to the first reason, why is the claim of eternal bodies denied?
A) Because eternity is full of events, and bodies lack events.
B) Because eternity is empty, which contradicts the observed changes in bodies.
C) Because observation shows bodies are eternal.
D) Because accidents are eternal.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi uses the observed fact that bodies are never free from accidents to argue that they cannot be eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If everything in your physical life is constantly changing and will eventually end, why do you still cling to people, possessions, and status as if they will last forever? What would it look like to truly live with the conviction that only Allah is eternal?
?
When you examine the history of your own life, you can count many 'beginnings'—your birth, your first job, your marriage, your children. If every new beginning is a sign that you are not eternal, how does that reality shape your priorities for the time you have left?
?
Maturidi argues that observation alone shows bodies are not eternal. Look at your own body right now: it is aging, changing, and dependent. Does your daily routine reflect a genuine belief that you will one day cease to exist, or do you live as if you have an infinite number of tomorrows? What is one habit you must change to prepare for your certain end?

Refuting Alternative Explanations and the Need for a Form-Giver
Maturidi refutes latency and scattering, and argues from form to a form-giver.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi rejects latency as an explanation for the origin of bodies and how he argues for a necessary form-giver.

Core Idea
Latency is absurd; every observed form needs a form-giver.

After presenting his two main arguments, Maturidi addresses counterarguments that might be used to preserve the eternity of bodies. He refutes the ideas of latency and scattering, showing they contradict observation and lead to absurdities. Then he provides a final proof: because every observed thing has a form, there must be a form-giver — pointing to the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the rebuttal
Read the passage carefully, focusing on the alternatives Maturidi rejects and his final argument.
Notice the phrases 'كان كامنا فظهر' and 'متفرقا فاجتمع'.
2
Understand the rejection of latency
Maturidi says it is not permissible to say bodies were latent and then appeared, because that would contradict observation.
Latency (kumun) is the idea that something exists in a hidden state within another thing.
3
Follow the logical consequence
If latency were accepted, it would open the possibility that the world came from nothing, which is absurd. Also, latency is impossible because one thing cannot become a place for many like it.
Think about the example: one thing cannot contain ten things of the same size.
4
Grasp the argument from form
Maturidi concludes that since every observed thing has a form, it cannot be free from a form-giver (musawwir). This implies a creator.
This argument is similar to the cosmological argument from design.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن يقول بقدم الأعيان فوجدناها غير خالية عن الحوادث لمنع القبول بذلك لوجوه: أحدها في القدم خلاء، وفي ذلك تكذيب شهادة العيان، والثاني وجود كثير من الأعيان وابتداؤها لمدد تعد، وهي من آخر الجملة تحتمل ما يحتمل الكل لذلك لزم القول، ولم يجز أن يقال: كان كامنا فظهر أو متفرقا فاجتمع لما فيه إثبات غير حكم العيان، وإذا احتمل ذلك، وإن ارتفع عن الإحاملة به، احتمل كون العالم من لا شيء، وإن ارتفع وجوده عن توهم البشر بدليل، والكمون لا يحتمل لإحالة كون شيء واحد مكانا لعشرة مثله، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ولما لا يخلو العيان وصفته من صور، ثم لا يخلو من مصور.
And whoever says that entities are eternal, we find them not free from accidents, which prevents acceptance of that, for several reasons: one is that in eternity there is emptiness, and in that is a denial of the testimony of observation; the second is the existence of many entities and their beginning at countable periods, and they are from the end of the aggregate and are subject to what the whole is subject to, therefore the statement is necessary. And latency is not possible because it is inconceivable that one thing becomes a place for ten things like it. And there is no power except with God. And since observation and its description are never free from forms, then they are never free from a form-giver.
Source pages p. 716

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that bodies (entities) are eternal (qadim). Maturidi argues that we observe bodies are never free from accidents (hawadith), which are temporal. Therefore, they cannot be eternal. He gives two reasons: (1) Eternity is empty of temporal events, but we see bodies changing, so observation contradicts eternity. كمون (latency)
مصور (form-giver)
العيان (observation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that bodies could have existed in a latent state before appearing, preserving eternity.
Correction: Maturidi shows that latency is impossible because it would require one thing to contain many, and it contradicts observation.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi reject the explanation that bodies were latent and then appeared?
A) Because latency is supported by observation.
B) Because latency would require one thing to be a place for many, which is impossible.
C) Because all bodies are eternal.
D) Because latency is mentioned in scripture.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes latency as an absurdity and proves that every observed form necessitates a form-giver, pointing to God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see order and form in your own life—your body, your daily routine—do you ever stop and ask who gave it that form? Or do you drift through as if it all happened by chance?
?
Maturidi says latency is absurd because one thing cannot contain ten like it. What 'absurdities' have you accepted about God's existence that, upon reflection, crumble under the weight of simple logic?
?
If every observed form requires a form-giver, what does that mean for your own existence right now? Are you living as if you have no Shaper, no Purpose behind your shape?

The Argument from Ignorance for a Wise Creator
Maturidi argues from creatures' ignorance to a wise creator and refutes pre-eternity of the universe.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the inherent ignorance of created things as a universal proof for the existence of a wise and powerful creator.

Core Idea
Creatures know their own ignorance — this points to a wise creator who knows all.

Maturidi presents a subtle argument: every created thing is aware of its own inability and ignorance regarding its benefit. This universal state of ignorance cannot be self-sufficient; it demands an all-knowing guide. In this passage, Maturidi builds on this to affirm the attributes of power and pre-eternal knowledge in the Maker, refuting the notion of a pre-eternal universe.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the starting observation
Understand that every thing knows its own inability and ignorance concerning its welfare. Maturidi begins by stating this as a given.
2
Identify the universal proof
See how Maturidi deems this ignorance a 'universal proof' (دليل الكلية) for a wise creator who directs each thing to its benefit.
This proof is foundational for the rest of the argument.
3
Examine the implications for divine attributes
Note how Maturidi connects this to power (قدرة) in pre-eternity (أزل) and generosity (جود), and that the Maker must be described with these attributes.
4
Contrast with the hypothesis of pre-eternity
Understand why a pre-eternal universe would negate divine attributes: if the whole were pre-eternal, God's power and action would be removed from temporal events.
This refutes the idea of an eternal world.
5
Conclude with the nature of takwin
Grasp that God's bringing-into-being (تكوين) is eternal and based on His knowledge: everything occurs as He knew it would, and He eternally wills it.
This preserves God's transcendence above temporality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما كان كل شيء يعلم من نفسه عجزه وجهله بأحواله وما فيه صلاحه، فيكون ذلك دليل الكلية، وغير ذلك من الأدلة التي تقدم ذكرها. ثم وصف الصانع بالقدرة في الأزل والجود لازم، وكذلك عندنا بالصنع ليكون كل على ما كان، ويكون أبد الآبدين على ارتفاع القدم عن كل كائن به لأنه نوع الفناء، وإحالة معنى التكوين عنه؛ إذ هو الكون نفسه وعلى ما كان ما لا تخلو الأنميان من الحوادث التي طريقها القدرة والكرم، ثم رجعت إلى الحوادث على ما يحتمل ذلك، فمثله الأعيان، ولا قوة إلا الله. ولو كان الكل قديما لكان وصف القدرة والفعل يزول عنه في الحادث، بل كان تكوينه أن يكون كل شيء على ما علم أن يكون ويريد بتكوين لم يزل به موصوفا؛ إذ هو يتعالى عن الحوادث فيه بما يصير بمعنى العالم الذي دل إحاطة الأحداث به على حدثه، فمثله الصانع والله الموفق.
Since every thing knows from itself its inability and ignorance of its states and what is its benefit, that is a universal proof, and other proofs previously mentioned. Then the description of the Maker with power in pre-eternity and generosity is necessary, and likewise according to us with making so that everything is as it was, and it will be forever upon the removal of pre-eternity from every thing coming-to-be by Him because it is a type of annihilation, and the impossibility of the meaning of bringing-into-being from Him; for it is coming-to-be itself and upon what it was, the entities [؟] are not free from events whose path is power and generosity, then they return to events according to what that permits, and likewise the entities, and there is no power except with God. And if the whole were pre-eternal, the description of power and action would be removed from Him in the temporal event, but rather His bringing-into-being is that everything is as He knew it would be, and He wills with a bringing-into-being never ceasing to be described by it; for He is exalted above events in it by becoming in the sense of the Knower, which the encompassing of events indicates its temporality, and likewise the Maker. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 717

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the existence of a wise and powerful creator based on the inherent ignorance of created things. Maturidi observes that every created thing is aware of its own inability and ignorance regarding what is beneficial for it. This serves as a universal proof that there must be an all-knowing creator who directs them. He then argues that the description of the Maker includes power in pre-eternity and generosity, and that He creates things in a manner consistent with His eternal knowledge. If the whole universe were pre-eternal, then the attributes of power and action attributed to God with respect to temporal events would be meaningless. Instead, God's bringing-into-being (takwin) is such that everything occurs exactly as He knew it would, and He eternally wills it. The fact that events encompass created things demonstrates their temporality (huduth), and similarly, the Maker is proven. The argument concludes that just as the temporality of events indicates a temporal world, the Maker is known through His acts.

Key Terms
عجز (inability)
جهل (ignorance)
صلاح (benefit)
القدرة (power)
الأزل (pre-eternity)
التكوين (bringing-into-being)
الحدث (temporality)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the ignorance of creatures proves they have no purpose or that there is no guiding intelligence.
Correction: Maturidi uses the fact that creatures are aware of their own ignorance as a universal proof that there must be an all-knowing creator who directs them to their benefit. Their ignorance points to a greater purpose set by a wise creator.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the fact that creatures are ignorant of their own benefit prove?
A) That they are not truly existing
B) That there must be an all-knowing creator who directs them
C) That they are free to choose their own benefit
D) That their benefit is determined by nature alone

Key Takeaway
The inherent ignorance of created things about their own benefit serves as a universal proof for the existence of an all-knowing and wise Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You admit that you are ignorant of your own true benefit and the full consequences of your actions. In which areas of your life do you most clearly feel this ignorance? How does this realization push you to rely on Allah's guidance in your daily decisions?
?
Maturidi says that your awareness of your own ignorance is a universal proof of a wise Creator. When you feel lost or uncertain about a major life choice, do you actually turn to the One who knows all? Or do you rely on your own limited understanding? What would change if you truly believed that Allah knows your benefit better than you do?
?
The passage teaches that everything comes from God's eternal bringing-into-being, exactly as He knew and willed. If you truly internalized that every moment of your life is precisely ordained by Allah's knowledge and will, what worries or anxieties would dissolve? What would you stop fearing?

Critique of Dahrīs: Co-eternal Entities Nullify Tawhid
Maturidi refutes the Dahrīs who make all entities co-eternal with God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Dahrīs' affirmation of the Creator's pre-eternity along with all entities undermines tawhid.

Core Idea
Affirming the Creator but making all things co-eternal is a subtle form of shirk.

Maturidi identifies a dangerous error within a group that nominally affirms the Creator. The Dahrīs accept that God is pre-eternal, but then they assign the same pre-eternity to all other entities. This passage shows that such a belief effectively nullifies the core Islamic principle of tawhid. Let's examine Maturidi's concise refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read Maturidi's critique
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice that Maturidi does not deny their belief in the Creator, but points out their fatal error.
The Dahrīs are not atheists; they affirm God.
2
Identify the doctrinal mistake
Maturidi says they 'place with Him all entities in pre-eternity'. What does this imply about their concept of God?
They deny the absolute uniqueness of God in pre-eternity.
3
Connect to tawhid
Maturidi concludes that this nullifies tawhid. Why? Because tawhid requires that only God is eternal without beginning. Any partner in pre-eternity breaks that.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذلك نحو من يقول من الدهرية بالبارى وقدم البارى فجعل معه جميع الأعيان في الأزل، وفى ذلك إبطال التوحيد . ومن يقول بالطينة والهيولى فيجعلها واحدا ثم أتلفه وجعل ما لا يحصى على الانتقال والفناء.
And that is like he who says among the Dahrīs of the Creator and the pre-eternity of the Creator, so he places with Him all entities in pre-eternity, and in that is the nullification of tawhid. And he who says of clay and prime matter makes them one, then eliminates it and made what cannot be counted upon transition and annihilation.
Source pages p. 718

Commentary
This passage criticizes two groups: the Dahrīs (materialists) who affirm the Creator and His pre-eternity but then posit that all individual entities are also co-eternal with Him, thereby violating tawhid by associating partners in pre-eternity. The second group believes in an eternal prime matter (al-ṭīna wa al-hayūlā) which they treat as one eternal thing, but then it undergoes change and becomes countless objects that perish, thus undermining the unique pre-eternity of God.

Key Terms
الدهرية
البارى
القدم
الأزل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Dahrīs are atheists who deny God entirely.
Correction: Maturidi shows they affirm the Creator but commit shirk by making all things co-eternal with Him.

Checkpoint
How do the Dahrīs nullify tawhid according to Maturidi?
A) By denying God
B) By making all things co-eternal with God
C) By believing in prime matter
D) By rejecting creation

Key Takeaway
The Dahrīs nullify tawhid by granting pre-eternity to all entities alongside God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself affirming God's existence but subtly treating something else—like your health, wealth, or reputation—as if it has always been there and always will be, independent of Him? How does the Dahrī error expose that hidden shirk in your own heart?
?
If the Dahrīs nullified tawhid by granting pre-eternity to all entities alongside God, what 'eternal' loves or fears in your life are you holding as co-eternal with God? What would it actually cost you to strip them of that false eternity and place God alone as the only Eternal?
?
This lesson reveals that even belief in God can be corrupted. Examine your own tawhid: are there any areas where you acknowledge God but refuse to let go of the idea that something else—your family, your security, your plans—is also self-sufficient and everlasting? What step can you take today to dethrone that idol?

Critique of Prime Matter Believers: Eternal Matter That Perishes
Maturidi refutes those who believe in an eternal prime matter that later changes and perishes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of those who posit an eternal prime matter that later transforms into perishable objects.

Core Idea
Believing in eternal prime matter undermines God's unique pre-eternity.

Maturidi now turns to another group: those who affirm an eternal prime matter (al-ṭīna wa al-hayūlā) as a single eternal substance, but then claim it undergoes change into countless perishable objects. This passage exposes the incoherence of making something eternal and then subject to change and annihilation.

Guided Path
1
Read Maturidi's critique
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the progression: they make it one, then eliminate it, then make countless things that transition and perish.
2
Analyze the logical problem
If prime matter is eternal and one, how can it become many and perishable? This contradicts the nature of the eternal.
The eternal cannot change or cease.
3
Recognize the theological implication
By positing an eternal matter alongside God, they compromise God's unique eternity. Maturidi implicitly shows this is another form of shirk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذلك نحو من يقول من الدهرية بالبارى وقدم البارى فجعل معه جميع الأعيان في الأزل، وفى ذلك إبطال التوحيد . ومن يقول بالطينة والهيولى فيجعلها واحدا ثم أتلفه وجعل ما لا يحصى على الانتقال والفناء.
And that is like he who says among the Dahrīs of the Creator and the pre-eternity of the Creator, so he places with Him all entities in pre-eternity, and in that is the nullification of tawhid. And he who says of clay and prime matter makes them one, then eliminates it and made what cannot be counted upon transition and annihilation.
Source pages p. 718

Commentary
This passage criticizes two groups: the Dahrīs (materialists) who affirm the Creator and His pre-eternity but then posit that all individual entities are also co-eternal with Him, thereby violating tawhid by associating partners in pre-eternity. The second group believes in an eternal prime matter (al-ṭīna wa al-hayūlā) which they treat as one eternal thing, but then it undergoes change and becomes countless objects that perish, thus undermining the unique pre-eternity of God.

الهيولى

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Affirmation of Correct Tawhid: God’s Unique Essence and Transcendence
Maturidi summarizes the correct doctrine of tawhid in positive attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's concise formulation of correct tawhid, including the unique nature of God's essence, His transcendence above limitations, and His essential attributes.

Core Idea
God's oneness is unique, not numerical; He transcends all limitations and is described by pre-eternity and power.

After refuting various erroneous sects, Imam al-Maturidi here presents the positive doctrine of tawhid in a single, tightly packed sentence. This formulation affirms God's unique essence, negates all anthropomorphic and limiting qualities, and establishes the essential attributes that truly describe Him. Let's unpack this rich statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation. Let the words sink in.
Notice the compressed style—every phrase carries theological weight.
2
Identify the three parts
The passage has three main parts: affirmation of essence (unique oneness), negations (of number, change, limitation), and positive attributes (pre-eternity, power, origination).
3
Understand 'wāḥidī al-dhāt'
This phrase means God's essence is unique, not composed, and not subject to quantity. It is different from saying 'one' in a numerical sense.
The common misunderstanding is that this implies atomism.
4
Reflect on the negations
Why are negations of number, change, and limitation necessary? They safeguard God's transcendence and prevent anthropomorphism.
Each negation protects a different aspect of tawhid.
5
Note the essential attributes
The passage mentions three attributes: qidam (pre-eternity), takwīn (origination), and qudra (power). These are fundamental for understanding God's relationship to creation.
These are not exhaustive, but key in Maturidi's system.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فحصل قول فريق بالتوحيد أنه واحدى الذات ، إليه حاجات الآحاد ، متعال عن معنى الآحاد عما يوجب صفة الأعداد ويتنكن فيه صفة التغير والزوال أو المحدود والنهاية ، موصوف بالقدم والتكوين والقدرة جل وعز عن التغير والزوال، والحمد لله على كل حال ..
So the correct statement of a group concerning tawhid is that He is unique in essence (wāḥidī al-dhāt), to Him are the needs of individuals, exalted above the meaning of individuals, above what necessitates the attribute of numbers, and cannot be entered by the attribute of change and passing away, nor of limitation and finitude. He is described by pre-eternity (qidam), bringing into existence (takwīn), and power (qudra). He is majestic and exalted above change and passing away. And praise be to Allah in every situation.
Source pages p. 720

Commentary
This passage is a positive statement of correct tawhid after refuting erroneous sects. Maturidi affirms that God is one in essence (wāḥidī al-dhāt), meaning His essence is unique and not composed. All individual beings (āḥād) are in need of Him. He is exalted above the concept of individuals (i.e., not part of a species or genus) and above anything that would imply numerical attributes (like being countable or having parts). The attributes of change (taghayyur), passing away (zawāl), limitation (ḥadd), and finitude (nihāya) cannot apply to Him. Instead, He is described by qidam (pre-eternity), takwīn (the power to originate existence), and qudra (power). He is absolutely transcendent above change and passing away. The passage ends with praise to Allah.

Key Terms
واحد الذات
آحاد
أعداد
تغير
زوال
محدود
نهاية
قدم
تكوين
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Saying 'wāḥidī al-dhāt' means God's essence is a simple indivisible atom.
Correction: It means His essence is unique and not composed; it does not imply atomism or any physical simplicity.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi mean by saying God is 'exalted above the meaning of individuals' (متعال عن معنى الآحاد)?
A) God does not know individuals.
B) God is not in need of anyone.
C) God is not a member of a genus or species.
D) God is alone with no creation.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's tawhid affirms God's unique, non-numerical oneness, negates all change and limitation, and establishes essential attributes of pre-eternity, power, and origination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God is beyond any limitation, or do you sometimes imagine Him in human terms? When you pray, do you think of Him as being confined to a direction or place? What specific thought can you replace with the affirmation of His transcendence?
?
The passage says all individuals are in need of Him (إليه حاجات الآحاد). Do you live as if you are entirely dependent on Him, or do you rely on your own abilities? In what area of your life do you need to consciously surrender to His power (qudra) today?
?
If God is described by pre-eternity (qidam), that means He has no beginning. Have you ever contemplated what it means for your own existence that you have a beginning and He does not? How should that difference shape your humility and worship?
